ASSERT(iter != connections_by_context_.end());\n    // To cover the lifetime of every single connection, Connections need to be deferred deleted\n    // because the previously contained connection is }\n  return *connections;\n}\n\nvoid OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase::removeFilterChain(const Network::FilterChain* filter_chain) {\n  auto iter = connections_by_context_.find(filter_chain);\n  if (iter If we have an\n      // upstream that is behaving badly, streams can get stuck here in the pending state. If we\n      // see a connect failure, we purge all pending streams so that calling code can determine\n      // what to do with the stream.\n      // NOTE: We move the existing pending streams to a temporary list. This is done so that\n      //       if retry logic submits a new stream to the pool, we don't fail it inline.\n      purgePendingStreams(client.real_host_description_, failure_reason, reason);\n      // See if we should preconnect based on active connections.\n      if (!is_draining_for_deletion_) {\n        tryCreateNewConnections();\n      }\n    }\n\n    // We need to release our resourceManager() resources before checking below for\n    // whether we can create a new connection. If the connection stays on the same worker, an\n`ActiveTcpSocket` is created and handed to `ActiveStreamListenerBase::onSocketAccepted()`.\n\n### How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?\n\n`ActiveTcpSocket::continueFilterChain()` runs any configured **listener filters**\n(e.g. `TLS Inspector`, `HTTP Inspector`) via `(*iter_)->onAccept(*this)`. When all listener filters\nhave passed, `ActiveTcpSocket::newConnection()` is called\n(`source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc:185`), which calls\n`ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`.\n\nInside `newConnection()`\n(`source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc:38`), the filter chain is selected\nby calling:\n```cpp\nconst auto filter_chain = config_->filterChainManager().findFilterChain(*socket, *stream_info);\n```\n`FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()`\n(`source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:514`) walks a multi-level trie in\npriority order:\n\n1. **Destination port** → `destination_ports_map_`\n2. **Destination IP / CIDR** → `findFilterChainForDestinationIP()` (`:563`)\n3. **Server name (SNI)** → `findFilterChainForServerName()` (`:580`)\n4. **Transport protocol** → `findFilterChainForTransportProtocol()` (`:611`)\n5. **Application protocol (ALPN)** → `findFilterChainForApplicationProtocols()` (`:631`)\n6. **Source IP / port** → `findFilterChainForSourceIpAndPort()` (`:702`)\n\nIf a matcher-based config is present, `findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` (`:549`) is used instead.\n\n### At what point does the connection get handed to the HCM?\n\nAfter `findFilterChain()` returns a non-null `FilterChain`, `newConnection()` calls:\n```cpp\nconfig_->filterChainFactory().createNetworkFilterChain(*server_conn_ptr,\n                                                        filter_chain->networkFilterFactories());\n```\n(`active_stream_listener_base.cc:68`)\n\nThis instantiates the HCM (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) as a `ReadFilter` and registers it on the\n`ServerConnectionImpl` via `FilterManagerImpl::addReadFilter()`\n(`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.cc:25`). The HCM implements the `Network::ReadFilter`\ninterface and exposes `onNewConnection()` and `onData()`.\n\n### What triggers the initial `onData()` call when bytes arrive?\n\nWhen the OS signals the socket is readable, `ConnectionImpl`'s libevent file-event callback fires.\n`ConnectionImpl::onReadReady()` (`source/common/network/connection_impl.cc:699`) calls\n`transport_socket_->doRead()` to drain the socket into `read_buffer_`, then calls\n`ConnectionImpl::onRead()` (`:394`), which calls `FilterManagerImpl::onRead()`\n(`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.cc:100`). `FilterManagerImpl::onRead()` calls\n`onContinueReading()` (`:62`) which iterates the upstream filter list and calls\n`filter->onData(read_buffer, end_stream)` on each active filter (`:92`). For the HCM this invokes\n`ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()`.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration\n\n### How does the codec parse the byte stream into HTTP headers/body?\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl::onData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool)` is the entry point\n(`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:486`). On first call it lazily creates the codec via\n`createCodec(data)` (`:465`) which calls `config_->createCodec()` and stores the result in\n`codec_`. For HTTP/1.1, this produces an `Http1::ServerConnectionImpl`.\n\n`codec_->dispatch(data)` is called in a loop (`:503`). The HTTP/1.1 codec\n(`source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc`) uses a BalsaParser/LLHTTP parser. Parsed events map to\ncallbacks:\n- `onMessageBeginBase()` (`:1266`) — called when the HTTP request-line is received. It creates\n  `ActiveRequest` and immediately calls `callbacks_.newStream(active_request_->response_encoder_)`\n  (`:1270`), which returns a `RequestDecoder&`.\n- `onUrlBase()` / header callbacks — accumulate URL and headers.\n- The full headers are dispatched to `request_decoder_->decodeHeaders(...)` once the header block\n  ends.\n- `onBody()` (`:1290`) calls `request_decoder_->decodeData(data, false)`.\n- The end of the request triggers `decodeData(data, true)`.\n\n### When is the `ActiveStream` created and how does it relate to filter iteration?\n\n`ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder, bool is_internally_created)`\n(`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:387`) creates a `std::unique_ptr<ActiveStream>` (`:407`),\nwires it to the `ResponseEncoder`, and `moveIntoList`s it onto `streams_`. The `ActiveStream` owns\nan `Http::FilterManager` which holds the ordered decoder-filter and encoder-filter lists.\n\nWhen the codec calls `request_decoder->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)`, this invokes\n`FilterManager::decodeHeaders()`, which iterates decoder filters.\n\n### How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?\n\n`FilterManager` maintains `decoder_filters_` as a `std::list<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr>` built\nin insertion order by `addStreamDecoderFilter()`. Filters are added in configuration order during\n`createFilterChain()` (HCM config). Iteration starts from the front (first configured filter) via\n`commonDecodePrefix()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:537`), which picks either the current\nfilter or the next one depending on `FilterIterationStartState`.\n\n`FilterManager::decodeHeaders(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter* filter, RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream)`\n(`:537`) drives the loop, calling `(*entry)->decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:555`) on each\nactive decoder filter entry.\n\n### What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?\n\n`FilterHeadersStatus` return values from `decodeHeaders`:\n\n| Value | Effect |\n|---|---|\n| `Continue` | Advance to next decoder filter |\n| `StopIteration` | Pause at current filter (`StopSingleIteration`), resume via `continueDecoding()` |\n| `StopAllIterationAndBuffer` | Buffer data and stop all iteration |\n| `StopAllIterationAndWatermark` | As above but also apply watermark pressure |\n| `ContinueAndDontEndStream` | Continue but clear `end_stream` (converts header-only to header+body) |\n\nThese are handled in `ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback()`\n(`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:130`).\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection\n\n### How does the router determine which route configuration to use?\n\nWhen the router filter (`Router::Filter`) receives `decodeHeaders()`, it calls:\n```cpp\nroute_ = callbacks_->route();\n```\n(`source/common/router/router.cc:468`)\n\n`callbacks_->route()` asks the `ActiveStream`'s route cache, which in turn consults the\n`RouteConfigProvider` (RDS or static). `RouteConfigImpl::route()` performs virtual-host lookup by\n`Host` header, then route matching against the path/method/headers, returning a `RouteEntry*`.\n\n### What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?\n\n1. `route_entry_ = route_->routeEntry()` — extract the `RouteEntry` (`:506`).\n2. `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` — look up the\n   `ThreadLocalCluster` by name from `ClusterManager` (`:519`).\n3. `cluster_ = cluster->info()` — snapshot the cluster's `ClusterInfo` (`:530`).\n4. `cluster->chooseHost(this)` — run the load-balancer to pick an `Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr`\n   (`:664`). This invokes the cluster's `LoadBalancer` (e.g. RoundRobin, LeastRequest) using the\n   `LoadBalancerContext` provided by the router filter.\n5. `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` — obtain or create a `GenericConnPool` (`:724`).\n\n### How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?\n\n`cluster->chooseHost(this)` delegates to the cluster's thread-local `LoadBalancer::chooseHost()`.\nThe load balancer selects from `ready` host entries in the cluster's priority set, applying the\nconfigured policy (round-robin, least-request, random, etc.) along with health-check and\nlocality-weight information. The result is a `HostConstSharedPtr`.\n\n### What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?\n\n`Filter::createConnPool()` (`source/common/router/router.cc:905`) calls\n`factory->createGenericConnPool(host, cluster, upstream_protocol, ...)` (`:946`). For HTTP upstreams\nthis constructs an `HttpConnPool`\n(`source/extensions/upstreams/http/http/upstream_request.h:21`), which wraps a\n`ThreadLocalCluster::httpConnPool()` handle.\n\nThen in `continueDecodeHeaders()` (`:714`), an `UpstreamRequest` is created and\n`UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:380`) is\ncalled, which calls `conn_pool_->newStream(this)` (`:404`). This either attaches to an existing\nready connection or enqueues a pending stream and calls\n`ConnPoolImplBase::tryCreateNewConnections()` → `tryCreateNewConnection()` →\n`instantiateActiveClient()`, creating a new `ActiveClient` and a TCP connection to the upstream\nhost (`source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:182`).\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow\n\n### How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?\n\n`ConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()` (`source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:294`) checks\n`ready_clients_` first:\n- **Pool hit**: calls `attachStreamToClient()` (`:203`), which calls `onPoolReady()`.\n- **Pool miss**: calls `newPendingStream()` to enqueue the request (`:327`), then\n  `tryCreateNewConnections()` → `tryCreateNewConnection()` (`:164`) → `instantiateActiveClient()`\n  (`:182`) which creates a new TCP connection via the host's connection factory.\n\nWhen the TCP connection completes the handshake, `ConnPoolImplBase::onConnectionEvent()` is\ntriggered. The `HttpConnPoolImplBase::onPoolReady()` (`source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:84`)\nis called: it calls `http_client->newStreamEncoder(response_decoder)` (`:90`), which for HTTP/1.1\ncalls `codec_client_->newStream(response_decoder)` returning an `Http::RequestEncoder&`. Then\n`callbacks.onPoolReady(new_encoder, ...)` is called.\n\nFor HTTP/1.1 (`Http::Http1::ActiveClient`):\n- `newStreamEncoder()` creates `StreamWrapper` which wraps the `RequestEncoderImpl` from the codec.\n\nFor the mixed pool (`HttpConnPoolImplMixed`) when no ALPN is available, a TCP `ActiveTcpClient` is\nfirst connected; after connection the pool checks ALPN and promotes to `Http1::ActiveClient` or\n`Http2::ActiveClient` (`source/common/http/mixed_conn_pool.cc:29`).\n\n### What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?\n\nThe call chain is:\n1. `HttpConnPool::onPoolReady()` creates an `HttpUpstream`\n   (`source/extensions/upstreams/http/http/upstream_request.cc:58`) wrapping the\n   `Http::RequestEncoder*`.\n2. `UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady()` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:584`) stores the\n   `HttpUpstream` and flushes any latched request data.\n3. The upstream HTTP filter chain is driven via `UpstreamFilterManager`. The terminal filter is\n   `UpstreamCodecFilter` (`source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc`).\n4. `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` (`:55`) calls\n   `callbacks_->upstreamCallbacks()->upstream()->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:64`).\n5. `HttpUpstream::encodeHeaders()` delegates to\n   `request_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (header file `:72`).\n6. `Http1::RequestEncoderImpl::encodeHeaders()` (`source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc:444`)\n   serializes the request line and headers into the connection's write buffer via\n   `connection_.buffer().addFragments(...)`.\n7. The `ConnectionImpl` write loop flushes the buffer to the socket via\n   `transport_socket_->doWrite()`.\n\n### How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?\n\n1. When the upstream socket becomes readable, the upstream `CodecClient` receives data in\n   `transport_socket_->doRead()`.\n2. The HTTP/1.1 parser fires `decodeHeaders()` / `decodeData()` on the registered\n   `ResponseDecoder`, which is the `Http1::ActiveClient::StreamWrapper`\n   (`source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.cc:26`), a `ResponseDecoderWrapper`.\n3. `StreamWrapper::decodeHeaders()` (`:41`) eventually delegates to `ResponseDecoderWrapper` →\n   the actual `ResponseDecoder`, which is `UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge`.\n4. `CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()` (`source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc:147`) calls\n   `filter_.callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` (`:189`), entering\n   the **upstream FilterManager** with encoder direction.\n5. The upstream `UpstreamFilterManager::encodeHeaders()` passes through upstream HTTP encoder\n   filters, then invokes the terminal `UpstreamToDownstream` bridge.\n6. `UpstreamRequest`'s `UpstreamToDownstream` forwards the call to the **downstream** HCM\n   `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1225`).\n7. Downstream encoder filters are iterated in reverse-configuration order. Each calls\n   `(*entry)->handle_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:1246`).\n8. After all encoder filters pass, `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` calls\n   `filter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders(headers, modified_end_stream)` (`:1305`), which is\n   `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:1771`).\n9. `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` calls `response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)`\n   (`:1924`) on the downstream `Http1::ResponseEncoderImpl`, serializing the response into the\n   downstream write buffer.\n\n### At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?\n\n| Phase | Filter Chain | Entry Point |\n|---|---|---|\n| Downstream request headers arrive | **Decoder** (downstream) | `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:537`) |\n| Downstream request body | **Decoder** (downstream) | `FilterManager::decodeData()` (`:638`) |\n| Upstream response headers arrive | **Encoder** (upstream HTTP filters) then **Encoder** (downstream) | `UpstreamFilterManager::encodeHeaders()` → `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:1225`) |\n| Upstream response body | **Encoder** (downstream) | `FilterManager::encodeData()` |\n| Request travels through upstream filter chain | **Decoder** (upstream HTTP filters) | `UpstreamFilterManager::decodeHeaders()` → `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` (`upstream_codec_filter.cc:55`) |\n\nThe encoder filter chain is the **mirror** of the decoder chain. Decoder filters run in\nconfiguration order (front-to-back) on incoming request data. Encoder filters run in\n**reverse** configuration order (back-to-front) on outgoing response data.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n| File | Lines | Subject |\n|---|---|---|\n| `RouteConfigImpl::route()` performs virtual-host lookup by\n`Host` header, then route matching against the path/method/headers, returning a `RouteEntry*`.\n\n### What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?\n\n1. `route_entry_ = route_->routeEntry()` — extract the `RouteEntry` (`:506`).\n2. `config_->cm_.getThreadLocalCluster(route_entry_->clusterName())` — look up the\n   `ThreadLocalCluster` by name from `ClusterManager` (`:519`).\n3. `cluster_ = cluster->info()` — snapshot the cluster's `ClusterInfo` (`:530`).\n4. `cluster->chooseHost(this)` — run the load-balancer to pick an `Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr`\n   (`:664`). This invokes the cluster's `LoadBalancer` (e.g. RoundRobin, LeastRequest) using the\n   `LoadBalancerContext` provided by the router filter.\n5. `createConnPool(*cluster, selected_host)` — obtain or create a `GenericConnPool` (`:724`).\n\n### How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?\n\n`cluster->chooseHost(this)` delegates to the cluster's thread-local `LoadBalancer::chooseHost()`.\nThe load balancer selects from `ready` host entries in the cluster's priority set, applying the\nconfigured policy (round-robin, least-request, random, etc.) along with health-check and\nlocality-weight information. The result is a `HostConstSharedPtr`.\n\n### What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?\n\n`Filter::createConnPool()` (`source/common/router/router.cc:905`) calls\n`factory->createGenericConnPool(host, cluster, upstream_protocol, ...)` (`:946`). For HTTP upstreams\nthis constructs an `HttpConnPool`\n(`source/extensions/upstreams/http/http/upstream_request.h:21`), which wraps a\n`ThreadLocalCluster::httpConnPool()` handle.\n\nThen in `continueDecodeHeaders()` (`:714`), an `UpstreamRequest` is created and\n`UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:380`) is\ncalled, which calls `conn_pool_->newStream(this)` (`:404`). This either attaches to an existing\nready connection or enqueues a pending stream and calls\n`ConnPoolImplBase::tryCreateNewConnections()` → `tryCreateNewConnection()` →\n`instantiateActiveClient()`, creating a new `ActiveClient` and a TCP connection to the upstream\nhost (`source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:182`).\n\n---\n\n## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow\n\n### How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?\n\n`ConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()` (`source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:294`) checks\n`ready_clients_` first:\n- **Pool hit**: calls `attachStreamToClient()` (`:203`), which calls `onPoolReady()`.\n- **Pool miss**: calls `newPendingStream()` to enqueue the request (`:327`), then\n  `tryCreateNewConnections()` → `tryCreateNewConnection()` (`:164`) → `instantiateActiveClient()`\n  (`:182`) which creates a new TCP connection via the host's connection factory.\n\nWhen the TCP connection completes the handshake, `ConnPoolImplBase::onConnectionEvent()` is\ntriggered. The `HttpConnPoolImplBase::onPoolReady()` (`source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:84`)\nis called: it calls `http_client->newStreamEncoder(response_decoder)` (`:90`), which for HTTP/1.1\ncalls `codec_client_->newStream(response_decoder)` returning an `Http::RequestEncoder&`. Then\n`callbacks.onPoolReady(new_encoder, ...)` is called.\n\nFor HTTP/1.1 (`Http::Http1::ActiveClient`):\n- `newStreamEncoder()` creates `StreamWrapper` which wraps the `RequestEncoderImpl` from the codec.\n\nFor the mixed pool (`HttpConnPoolImplMixed`) when no ALPN is available, a TCP `ActiveTcpClient` is\nfirst connected; after connection the pool checks ALPN and promotes to `Http1::ActiveClient` or\n`Http2::ActiveClient` (`source/common/http/mixed_conn_pool.cc:29`).\n\n### What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?\n\nThe call chain is:\n1. `HttpConnPool::onPoolReady()` creates an `HttpUpstream`\n   (`source/extensions/upstreams/http/http/upstream_request.cc:58`) wrapping the\n   `Http::RequestEncoder*`.\n2. `UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady()` (`source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:584`) stores the\n   `HttpUpstream` and flushes any latched request data.\n3. The upstream HTTP filter chain is driven via `UpstreamFilterManager`. The terminal filter is\n   `UpstreamCodecFilter` (`source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc`).\n4. `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` (`:55`) calls\n   `callbacks_->upstreamCallbacks()->upstream()->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:64`).\n5. `HttpUpstream::encodeHeaders()` delegates to\n   `request_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (header file `:72`).\n6. `Http1::RequestEncoderImpl::encodeHeaders()` (`source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc:444`)\n   serializes the request line and headers into the connection's write buffer via\n   `connection_.buffer().addFragments(...)`.\n7. The `ConnectionImpl` write loop flushes the buffer to the socket via\n   `transport_socket_->doWrite()`.\n\n### How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?\n\n1. When the upstream socket becomes readable, the upstream `CodecClient` receives data in\n   `transport_socket_->doRead()`.\n2. The HTTP/1.1 parser fires `decodeHeaders()` / `decodeData()` on the registered\n   `ResponseDecoder`, which is the `Http1::ActiveClient::StreamWrapper`\n   (`source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.cc:26`), a `ResponseDecoderWrapper`.\n3. `StreamWrapper::decodeHeaders()` (`:41`) eventually delegates to `ResponseDecoderWrapper` →\n   the actual `ResponseDecoder`, which is `UpstreamCodecFilter::CodecBridge`.\n4. `CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()` (`source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc:147`) calls\n   `filter_.callbacks_->encodeHeaders(std::move(headers), end_stream, ...)` (`:189`), entering\n   the **upstream FilterManager** with encoder direction.\n5. The upstream `UpstreamFilterManager::encodeHeaders()` passes through upstream HTTP encoder\n   filters, then invokes the terminal `UpstreamToDownstream` bridge.\n6. `UpstreamRequest`'s `UpstreamToDownstream` forwards the call to the **downstream** HCM\n   `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1225`).\n7. Downstream encoder filters are iterated in reverse-configuration order. Each calls\n   `(*entry)->handle_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)` (`:1246`).\n8. After all encoder filters pass, `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` calls\n   `filter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders(headers, modified_end_stream)` (`:1305`), which is\n   `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` (`source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc:1771`).\n9. `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders()` calls `response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)`\n   (`:1924`) on the downstream `Http1::ResponseEncoderImpl`, serializing the response into the\n   downstream write buffer.\n\n### At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?\n\n| Phase | Filter Chain | Entry Point |\n|---|---|---|\n| Downstream request headers arrive | **Decoder** (downstream) | `FilterManager::decodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:537`) |\n| Downstream request body | **Decoder** (downstream) | `FilterManager::decodeData()` (`:638`) |\n| Upstream response headers arrive | **Encoder** (upstream HTTP filters) then **Encoder** (downstream) | `UpstreamFilterManager::encodeHeaders()` → `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (`filter_manager.cc:1225`) |\n| Upstream response body | **Encoder** (downstream) | `FilterManager::encodeData()` |\n| Request travels through upstream filter chain | **Decoder** (upstream HTTP filters) | `UpstreamFilterManager::decodeHeaders()` → `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` (`upstream_codec_filter.cc:55`) |\n\nThe encoder filter chain is the **mirror** of the decoder chain. Decoder filters run in\nconfiguration order (front-to-back) on incoming request data. Encoder filters run in\n**reverse** configuration order (back-to-front) on outgoing response data.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n| File | Lines | Subject |\n|---|---|---|\n|
